edX Support

For questions on course lectures, homework, tools, or materials for this course, post in the course discussion forum.

Have general questions about edX? You can find lots of helpful information in the edX FAQ.

Have a question about something specific? You can contact the edX general support team directly:

Please note: The edX support team is English speaking. While we will do our best to address your inquiry in any language, our responses will be in English.

Describe what you were doing when you encountered the issue. Include any details that will help us to troubleshoot, including error messages that you saw.

Thank You!

Thank you for your inquiry or feedback. We typically respond to a request within one business day, Monday to Friday. In the meantime, please review our detailed FAQs where most questions have already been answered.

It comes up heads every time. Which is correct?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 2&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;choicegroup capa_inputtype&#34; id=&#34;inputtype_d22e06d8c0e44921b5c71b9ab95442fe_3_1&#34;&gt;&lt;fieldset aria-describedby=&#34;status_d22e06d8c0e44921b5c71b9ab95442fe_3_1&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;field&#34;&gt;&lt;label id=&#34;d22e06d8c0e44921b5c71b9ab95442fe_3_1-choice_0-label&#34; class=&#34;response-label field-label label-inline&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;status_d22e06d8c0e44921b5c71b9ab95442fe_3_1&#34;&gt;&lt;input type=&#34;radio&#34; name=&#34;input_d22e06d8c0e44921b5c71b9ab95442fe_3_1[]&#34; class=&#34;response-label field-label label-inline choicegroup_correct&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;status_d22e06d8c0e44921b5c71b9ab95442fe_3_1&#34;&gt;&lt;input type=&#34;radio&#34; name=&#34;input_d22e06d8c0e44921b5c71b9ab95442fe_3_1[]&#34; id=&#34;status_d22e06d8c0e44921b5c71b9ab95442fe_3_1&#34; data-tooltip=&#34;This answer is correct.&#34;&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;sr&#34;&gt;correct&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;status-icon&#34; aria-hidden=&#34;true&#34;/&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/label&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span id=&#34;answer_d22e06d8c0e44921b5c71b9ab95442fe_3_1&#34;/&gt;&lt;/fieldset&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;indicator-container&#34;&gt; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Next we toss a huge ball with 1,000 dots on it. Half the dots are red and the other half are blue. We roll the ball and when it stops, we note the color of the dot on the very top of the ball.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;True or False? If we roll it four times, and it comes up red once and blue three times, then we have proved that the ball is biased.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; data-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.2x+3T2017+type@problem+block@adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382" > <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-problem xmodule_display xmodule_CapaModule" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="XBlockToXModuleShim" data-block-type="problem" data-request-token="f51b48c6d9a911e7b6f10e1739f92b74" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.2x+3T2017+type@problem+block@adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382" data-type="Problem" data-course-id="course-v1:MITx+6.00.2x+3T2017"> <script type="json/xblock-args" aria-labelledby="adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382-problem-title" data-problem-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.2x+3T2017+type@problem+block@adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382" data-url="/courses/course-v1:MITx+6.00.2x+3T2017/xblock/block-v1:MITx+6.00.2x+3T2017+type@problem+block@adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382/handler/xmodule_handler" data-problem-score="5.0" data-problem-total-possible="5.0" data-attempts-used="4" data-content=" &lt;h3 class=&#34;hd hd-3 problem-header&#34; id=&#34;adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382-problem-title&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.2x+3T2017+type@problem+block@adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382-problem-progress&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt; Exercise 3 &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.2x+3T2017+type@problem+block@adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;p&gt;Write a function, &lt;code&gt;stdDevOfLengths(L)&lt;/code&gt; that takes in a list of strings, &lt;code&gt;L&lt;/code&gt;, and outputs the standard deviation of the lengths of the strings. Return &lt;code&gt;float(&#39;NaN&#39;)&lt;/code&gt; if &lt;code&gt;L&lt;/code&gt; is empty.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Recall that the standard deviation is computed by this equation:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;[mathjax]\sqrt{\frac{\sum_{t\text{ in }X} (t - \mu)^2}{N}}[/mathjax]&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;where:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;[mathjaxinline]\mu[/mathjaxinline] is the mean of the elements in &lt;i&gt;X&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;[mathjaxinline]\sum_{t\text{ in }X} (t - \mu)^2[/mathjaxinline] means the sum of the quantity [mathjaxinline](t - \mu)^2[/mathjaxinline] for &lt;i&gt;t&lt;/i&gt; in &lt;i&gt;X&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;That is, for each element (that we name &lt;i&gt;t&lt;/i&gt;) in the set &lt;i&gt;X&lt;/i&gt;, we compute the quantity [mathjaxinline](t - \mu)^2[/mathjaxinline]. We then sum up all those computed quantities.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;N&lt;/i&gt; is the number of elements in &lt;i&gt;X&lt;/i&gt;. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Test case: If &lt;code&gt;L = [&#39;a&#39;, &#39;z&#39;, &#39;p&#39;]&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;stdDevOfLengths(L)&lt;/code&gt; should return 0.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Test case: If &lt;code&gt;L = [&#39;apples&#39;, &#39;oranges&#39;, &#39;kiwis&#39;, &#39;pineapples&#39;]&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;stdDevOfLengths(L)&lt;/code&gt; should return 1.8708.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&lt;p&gt;If you want to use numpy arrays, you should &lt;code&gt;import numpy as np&lt;/code&gt; and use &lt;code&gt;np.METHOD_NAME&lt;/code&gt; in your code.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;div id=&#34;textbox_adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382_2_1&#34; class=&#34;capa_inputtype textbox cminput&#34;&gt;&lt;label class=&#34;sr problem-group-label&#34; for=&#34;cm-textarea-adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382_2_1&#34;&gt;Code Editor&lt;/label&gt;&lt;textarea rows=&#34;30&#34; cols=&#34;80&#34; name=&#34;input_adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382_2_1&#34; aria-label=&#34;python editor&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;answer_adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382_2_1&#34; id=&#34;input_adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382_2_1&#34; tabindex=&#34;0&#34; data-mode=&#34;python&#34; data-tabsize=&#34;4&#34; data-linenums=&#34;true&#34;&gt;import math def stdDevOfLengths(L): &#34;&#34;&#34; L: a list of strings returns: float, the standard deviation of the lengths of the strings, or NaN if L is empty. &#34;&#34;&#34; if len(L) == 0: return float(&#39;NaN&#39;) s = 0 for l in L: s += len(l) mean = s / len(L) s = 0 for l in L: s += (len(l) - mean)**2 return math.sqrt(s/len(L)) # if __name__ == &#39;__main__&#39;: # print(stdDevOfLengths([&#39;a&#39;, &#39;z&#39;, &#39;p&#39;]) == 0) # print(stdDevOfLengths([&#39;apples&#39;, &#39;oranges&#39;, &#39;kiwis&#39;, &#39;pineapples&#39;]) == 1.8708286933869707)&lt;/textarea&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;cm-editor-exit-message capa-message&#34; id=&#34;cm-editor-exit-message-adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382_2_1&#34;&gt; Press ESC then TAB or click outside of the code editor to exit &lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;grader-status&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;status correct&#34; id=&#34;status_adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382_2_1&#34; data-tooltip=&#34;This answer is correct.&#34;&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;sr&#34;&gt;correct&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;status-icon&#34; aria-hidden=&#34;true&#34;/&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;p class=&#34;debug&#34;&gt;correct&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span id=&#34;answer_adb06698d16f44a2a2044163e398b382_2_1&#34;/&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;external-grader-message&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;test&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;Test edX Verified Certificate

Why upgrade?

  • Official proof of completion
  • Easily shareable certificate
  • Proven motivator to complete the course
  • Certificate purchases help edX continue to offer free courses

How it works

  • Pay the Verified Certificate upgrade fee
  • Verify your identity with a webcam and government-issued ID
  • Study hard and pass the course
  • Share your certificate with friends, employers, and others

  • Use the arrow keys to navigate the tips or use the tab key to return to the calculator

    For detailed information, see Entering Mathematical and Scientific Expressions in the edX Guide for Students.

  • Tips:

    • Use parentheses () to make expressions clear. You can use parentheses inside other parentheses.

    • Do not use spaces in expressions.

    • For constants, indicate multiplication explicitly (example: 5*c).

    • For affixes, type the number and affix without a space (example: 5c).

    • For functions, type the name of the function, then the expression in parentheses.

  • To Use Type Examples
    Numbers Integers
    Fractions
    Decimals     		2520
    2/3
    3.14, .98
    Operators + - * / (add, subtract, multiply, divide)
    ^ (raise to a power)
    || (parallel resistors)     		x+(2*y)/x-1 x^(n+1)
    v_IN+v_OUT
    1||2
    Constants c, e, g, i, j, k, pi, q, T 20*c
    418*T
    Affixes Percent sign (%) and metric affixes (d, c, m, u, n, p, k, M, G, T) 20%
    20c
    418T
    Basic functions abs, exp, fact or factorial, ln, log2, log10, sqrt abs(x+y)
    sqrt(x^2-y)
    Trigonometric functions sin, cos, tan, sec, csc, cot
    arcsin, sinh, arcsinh, etc.
    		 sin(4x+y)
    arccsch(4x+y)
    Scientific notation 10^ and the exponent 10^-9
    e notation 1e and the exponent 1e-9
